أن ما يمثل معقد اتفاق لديهم جميعاً أن للعلم أو المعرفة في القرآن مكانة خاصة تحفل بها كثير من آياته مما يعني توافقاً بين معطيات القرآن والعلم على نحو من التوازي لا التضاد. ذلك أن مصدر العطاء واحد هو الله - تعالى -(۱) .
وعلى سبيل المثال - لا الحصر - فإن العلماء مقرونون بالله تعالى وملائكته في بعض آيات القرآن الكريم كما في قوله سبحانه وشَهِدَ اللهُ أَنَّهُ لا إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ وَالْمَلائِكَةُ وَأُولُو الْعِلْمِ قَائِماً بِالْقِسْطِ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ الْعَزِيزُ الْحَكِيمُ [آل عمران: 18/3].
(۱) الإعجاز العلمي في القرآن والسنة). ويساند هذا الاتجاه مشترطاً عدم الاعتساف في فهم نصوصه ذات العلاقة بقضايا العلم محمد عبدالله دراز في كتابه (مدخل إلى القرآن، ۱۷۵ - ۱۷۷ الشيخ عبدالوهاب خلاف فلا يرى بأساً من تفسير القرآن علمياً، بل ولا يلتفت إلى ما يقال عن تبدل النظريات العلمية إذ يعد تفسير النص القرآني أحد وجوه الدلالة فقط فإذا ظهر خطأ النظرية ظهر خطأ فهم الآية (انظر: أصول الفقه، ۲۹ - ۳۰).
و ممن يشايع هذا الاتجاه أيضاً: الشيخ محمد متولي الشعراوي الذي يعتمده في تفسيره. (انظر: المختار من تفسير القرآن الجزء الأول ) والشيخ محمد الغزالي كيف نتعامل مع القرآن، ١٣٧ - ١٤٢ )، وحمودة محمد سند الإعجاز العلمي للقرآن والسنة ((النظرية والتطبيق))، ۸۷ - ۸۸ ) وعبدالمجيد النجار، في فقه التدين فهماً وتنزيلاً، ١٠٠/١ - ١٠٤ ).
تعليق والرأي الأنسب - فيما يبدو - التوسط، بحيث لا ينبغي إيقاف من الإعجاز العلمي للقرآن، لما له من فوائد جمة سواء على مستوى إظهار معجزات القرآن العلمية على غير المسلمين وبالأخص العلماء المعنيين منهم، فيدفعهم ذلك نحو قراءة القرآن والتفاعل معه بما قد يؤول إلى دخولهم الإسلام، أو على الأقل إنصافه واحترام أهله، أو على المستوى الداخلي في دائرة المؤمنين أنفسهم، إذ تتعزر الحقيقة الإيمانية في قلوبهم، على نحو أعمق إيماناً، وأرسخ يقيناً. بيد أن ذلك يجب أن يتقيد بحملة ضوابط منهجية لعل من أبرزها ما يلي:
١ - التروّي وعدم المسارعة إلى الإعلان عن كل جديد مكتشف حتى يصل إلى نتائجه النهائية غير القابلة للاختلاف أو التبدل.
- الاعتماد على اتجاه الإعجاز العلمي لتحقيق أهداف لا تتعارض ومنهج إسلام المعرفة، بحيث إنه لا ينبغي الارتكاز عليه تماماً، كما لو كان هو الاتجاه الوحيد في تفسير القرآن، أو له من الأفضلية ما يقلّل من شأن المناهج الأخرى.
٣- إن القول بهذا لا يبرر للمسلمين قعودهم عن ولوج عالم التقنية والاكتشافات ليكونوا هم السباقين بالفعل إلى الاكتشاف، ومن ثم مطابقته بما ورد في القرآن الكريم، لا أن يهتموا فقط بتلقط أخبار الاكتشافات العلمية، ثم ينقبوا في المصحف الشريف عن دلالات تطابقها، فإن هذا المسلك يعمق حالة العجز عند المسلمين، اكتفاء بحالة الرصد السلبي هذه، وذلك أحد ضـروب خداع الذات في حقيقة الأمر. (۱) عماد الدين خليل، مدخل إلى موقف القرآن الكريم من العلم، ۱۸ - ۲۰ ، وانظر: ١١٩ - ١٢٤ .
What represents a common ground among them all is that knowledge or cognition in the Quran has a special status, attended to by many of its verses, implying a parallelism, not contradiction, between the data of the Quran and science. That is because the source of giving is one: God Almighty (1). For example, not exclusively, scholars are mentioned in association with God and His angels in some verses of the Noble Quran, as in His saying: God bears witness that there is no god but He, and the angels and those of knowledge, standing in justice; there is no god but He, the Mighty, the Wise (Al-Imran 3:18). (1) Scientific Miracle in the Quran and Sunnah. This trend is supported, with the condition of not distorting the understanding of its texts related to scientific issues, by Muhammad Abdullah Draz in his book (Introduction to the Quran, 175-177), Sheikh Abdulwahhab Khallaf who sees no harm in interpreting the Quran scientifically, even disregarding what is said about the change of scientific theories, because interpreting the Quranic text is only one aspect of indication; if the theory is shown to be wrong, the misunderstanding of the verse becomes apparent (see: Usul al-Fiqh, 29-30). Also supporting this trend: Sheikh Muhammad Metwali al-Sha'rawi, who adopts it in his interpretation (see: al-Mukhtar min Tafsir al-Quran, part one), Sheikh Muhammad al-Ghazali (How to Deal with the Quran, 137-142), Hammouda Muhammad Sind (Scientific Miracle of the Quran and Sunnah (Theory and Practice), 87-88), and Abdulmajid al-Najjar (Fiqh al-Tadayyun Fahman wa Tanzilan, 1/100-104). Comment: the most appropriate opinion - it seems - is moderation, such that one should not cease from [pursuing] the scientific miracle of the Quran, because it has immense benefits, whether on the level of demonstrating the Quran's scientific miracles to non-Muslims, especially concerned scientists, motivating them to read and interact with the Quran, possibly leading to their entry into Islam, or at least fairness and respect for its people, or on the internal level within the circle of believers themselves, since the truth of faith becomes stronger in their hearts, deeper in faith and firmer in certainty. However, this must be bound by a set of methodological controls, the most prominent of which are: 1. Deliberation and not rushing to announce every new discovery until it reaches its final results that are not subject to dispute or change. 2. Relying on the trend of scientific miracle to achieve goals that do not conflict with the methodology of Islamic knowledge, such that one should not rely on it entirely, as if it were the only direction in interpreting the Quran, or that it has such superiority as to diminish the importance of other methodologies. 3. Saying this does not justify Muslims sitting back from entering the world of technology and discoveries to be the actual pioneers of discovery, and then matching it with what is in the Noble Quran, not just caring to pick up news of scientific discoveries, then digging in the Holy Book for indications that match them; for this path deepens the state of incapacity among Muslims, content with this negative observation, and this is one form of self-deception in reality. (1) Imad al-Din Khalil, Introduction to the Quran's Position on Science, 18-20, and see: 119-124.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents a discussion on the relationship between the Quran and science. The author first establishes a common ground: the Quran places a special emphasis on knowledge, and there is a parallel, not contradiction, between Quranic revelations and scientific findings, as both originate from God. To support this, the author cites examples such as the Quranic verse associating scholars with God and angels (Al-Imran 3:18). The author then lists scholars who advocate for scientific interpretation of the Quran under certain conditions, including Muhammad Abdullah Draz, Abdulwahhab Khallaf, and others. Following this, the author provides a commentary advocating a moderate approach: scientific interpretation of the Quran should not be abandoned because it has benefits for both non-Muslims and believers. However, it must be governed by three methodological controls. First, one must be deliberate and not rush to announce discoveries until they are settled. Second, the scientific miracle approach should not be made the exclusive or superior method of interpretation. Third, Muslims should not be passive observers but active participants in scientific discovery, matching their findings with the Quran rather than merely searching for confirmations. The author warns that passive observation leads to self-deception and deepens the state of incapacity.

Key Terms
العلم
المعرفة
الإعجاز العلمي
ضوابط منهجية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one of the methodological controls for scientific interpretation of the Quran?
A) It should be the exclusive method of interpretation.
B) Muslims should wait for non-Muslims to discover before confirming in Quran.
C) One should not rush to announce a new discovery until it is final and undisputed.
D) Scientific interpretation is only for non-Muslims.

Key Takeaway
A moderate approach to scientific miracles requires three controls: deliberation, balance, and active Islamic scientific participation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Choose a recent scientific discovery (e.g., embryology) that is often linked to the Quran. Apply the first control: Is the discovery final and undisputed? What would the author say about announcing it as a miracle?
?
Imagine a commentator who only uses scientific miracles to explain verses. Which control does that violate, and why?

Four Methodological Principles for Engaging with the Quran
Author outlines four methodological steps for engaging with the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the four methodological principles for engaging with the Quran as outlined in the passage.

Core Idea
The Quran itself is the key to understanding its own language and structure.

This lesson unpacks four foundational steps for approaching the Quran: understanding its linguistic nature, treating it as a structural unity, integrating revelation and cosmos, and adopting a conceptual reading. These steps ensure a comprehensive and contextual engagement with the Quranic text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four steps
List the four methodological principles given in the passage.
They are: 1) grasping the nature of Quranic language, 2) structural unity, 3) combining revelation and cosmos, 4) conceptual reading.
2
Analyze the linguistic principle
The passage says the language of the Quran must be understood from the historical horizon of the Bedouin to contemporary knowledge, using the Quran itself as source.
This implies a contextual and evolving understanding.
3
Analyze the structural unity principle
The Quran is described as a 'single body' that must be read in its own context as a comprehensive whole.
This discourages cherry-picking verses.
4
Analyze the third and fourth principles
The third calls for integrating revealed and empirical knowledge; the fourth emphasizes that Quranic language has a conceptual dimension valid across time and place.
They highlight the Quran's relevance to both spiritual and physical realms.
5
Connect to tafsir methodology
Consider how classical tafsir works (e.g., al-Tabari) embody these principles.
For instance, al-Tabari often discusses historical context and uses Quran as its own interpreter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١ - إدراك طبيعة لغة القرآن على نحو يمتد بها من أفق الفهم البدوي الذي تعامل به الأعرابي زمن نزول القرآن إلى أفق المعرفة في زماننا، وفق قراءة سياق الآيات تجعل من القرآن ذاته أهم مصدر لفهمه. -۲- وحدة القرآن البنائية على معنى أنه جسم واحد، يُقرأ في سياقه الخاص، بوصفه وحدة موضوعية تقرأ قراءة كلية شاملة. -٣- الجمع بين قراءة الوحي وقراءة الكون. - القراءة المفهوماتية: بمعنى أن لغة القرآن ذات بعد مفهومي يصلح لكل زمان ومكان، ولا يشترط ثباته على مدلول واحد عبر العصور، وفي مختلف الأمصار . (۱) علاقة المعرفة بالتربية تقوم عملية التربية على جملة من الأبنية النظامية المتسمة بالترابط والتسلسل والمنطقية. فثمة علاقة عضوية - على سبيل المثال - تربط المعرفة بالقراءة كخطوة أولى على طريق المسار التربوي، بحيث يصبح من نافلة القول التأكيد على أن القراءة مفتاح المعرفة، وأن المعرفة من غير القراءة ناقصة إلى حد يكاد يسقطها من وصف المعرفة - فضلاً عن المعرفة التربوية -. ومن غير المتصوّر قيام حضارة من غير امتلاك لمهارة القراءة، ومن ثم امتلاك لناصية المعرفة، إذ إن ذلك يخالف سنة حضارية لا فكاك منها. ومنذ بدأ الإنسان يقرأ ويكتب فقد بدأ يعرف ويعلم، وأضحى كل يوم في نماء معرفي مطرد باطراد قراءته (٢). ونظراً لما للقراءة من أهمية معرفية فقد بدأت رسالة الإسلام الخاتمة بكلمة (اقرأ)، ولم تبدأ بالأمر بالصوم، أو الصلاة، أو الزكاة، أو الجهاد، برغم أهمية ذلك كله
1- Grasping the nature of the language of the Quran in a way that extends from the horizon of primitive understanding with which the Bedouin dealt at the time of revelation to the horizon of knowledge in our time, according to a reading of the context of verses that makes the Quran itself the most important source for understanding it. 2- The structural unity of the Quran, meaning that it is single body, read in its own context, as an objective unit read as a comprehensive whole. 3- Combining the reading of revelation and the reading of the cosmos. 4- Conceptual reading: meaning that the language of the Quran has a conceptual dimension suitable for every time and place, and it is not required to remain fixed on one meaning across ages and in various regions. (1) The relationship between knowledge and education: The process of education is based on a set of systemic structures characterized by interconnectedness, sequence, and logic. There is an organic relationship, for example, linking knowledge to reading as a first step on the educational path, such that it becomes superfluous to emphasize that reading is the key to knowledge, and that knowledge without reading is deficient to the point that it almost falls from the description of knowledge—let alone educational knowledge. It is inconceivable to establish a civilization without possessing the skill of reading, and then possessing the reins of knowledge, for that contradicts an inevitable civilizational law. Since man began to read and write, he began to know and learn, and every day he has continued in steady cognitive growth proportional to his reading (2). And because of the cognitive importance of reading, the final message of Islam began with the word 'Iqra' (Read), and did not begin with the command to fast, pray, give zakat, or engage in jihad, despite the importance of all that.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage presents four methodological principles for engaging with the Quran. First, one must understand the linguistic nature of the Quran in a way that bridges the historical context of revelation with contemporary understanding, using the Quran itself as the primary source. Second, the Quran must be treated as a structural unity, read as a coherent whole rather than fragmented. Third, there must be an integration of revealed knowledge (reading of revelation) and empirical knowledge (reading of the cosmos). Fourth, the Quran's language has a conceptual dimension that transcends time and place, not bound to a single interpretation. The passage then transitions to discuss the relationship between knowledge and education, arguing that reading is the foundational skill for acquiring knowledge, and that civilization depends on literacy. The author notes that Islam's revelation began with the command 'Iqra' (Read), highlighting the primacy of reading over other acts of worship.

Key Terms
قراءة (qirāʾa): Reading, both literal and interpretive; the first revealed word and the key to knowledge. [Note: In Quranic exegesis, qirāʾa often refers to variant recitations; here it means engaged reading.]
تربية (tarbiya): Education, based on systemic structures and logically sequenced steps. [Note: Stable in Islamic educational discourse.]
إدراك طبيعة لغة القرآن
وحدة القرآن البنائية
الجمع بين قراءة الوحي وقراءة الكون
القراءة المفهوماتية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which principle emphasizes that the Quran should be read as a coherent whole?
A) Linguistic understanding
B) Structural unity
C) Combining revelation and cosmos
D) Conceptual reading

Key Takeaway
The Quran must be approached through a contextual, holistic, integrated, and flexible methodology that respects its linguistic and conceptual depth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Choose a short Quranic passage (e.g., Surah al-Fatiha). In light of the four principles, explain how you would approach its interpretation.

The Primacy of Reading in Islamic Education
Author outlines four methodological steps for engaging with the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate the relationship between reading, knowledge, and the Islamic educational system as presented in the passage.

Core Idea
Reading is the foundational skill for all knowledge and civilization, emphasized by the first revealed command 'Iqra'.

The passage argues that reading is not only the key to knowledge but also the basis for educational and civilizational development. It notes that the Islamic message began with 'Iqra', underscoring the cognitive importance of literacy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim about reading
What does the passage say about the relationship between reading and knowledge?
Reading is called the key to knowledge; knowledge without reading is deficient.
2
Analyze the educational implication
How does the passage describe the structure of education?
It mentions 'systemic structures', 'interconnectedness', 'sequence', and 'logic'.
3
Connect to the Islamic revelation
Why does the author highlight that the Quran began with 'Iqra'?
To show reading's cognitive importance; it was prioritized over worship acts.
4
Reflect on the civilizational argument
The passage claims civilization depends on reading. Evaluate this claim.
Consider historical examples like the Islamic Golden Age where literacy flourished.

Five Elements of Islamic Epistemology: Classification and Critique
Author presents a five-element classification and critiques its redundancy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five elements of Islamic epistemology proposed by one researcher and explain the author's critique that the classification is redundant.

Core Idea
Not all classifications are equally useful; redundancy can obscure real epistemological foundations.

This passage presents a contemporary attempt to classify the elements of Islamic epistemology into five components. However, the author immediately notes a significant problem: many of these elements are synonymous with each other, raising the question of whether such a classification is truly analytical or merely repetitive. Let us examine the classification and its critique carefully.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five elements
Locate the list in the Arabic text. The author enumerates five elements: sound intellect, the Quran, the universe, human heritage, and the process of digesting and representing these elements.
The fifth element is not a source itself but a method of internalizing the others.
2
Understand the author's critique
The author states that the first three elements (intellect, Quran, universe) are nearly synonymous with the sources and methods of knowledge. This means the classification is not truly differentiating between distinct epistemological categories.
The author does not reject the elements themselves but questions the logical coherence of listing them as separate.
3
Consider the alternative reduction
The passage mentions another researcher who reduces all elements to two: knowledge ('ilm) and faith (iman), with their organic necessities. This suggests a more streamlined epistemological framework.
This reduction implies that the five elements can be subsumed under these two overarching categories.
4
Evaluate the practical implication
Despite the critique, the author affirms the importance of digesting and representing these elements in human and educational reality. The classification, even if redundant, still points to the need for integrating multiple sources.
The critique does not negate the practical usefulness of the elements; it only questions their logical independence.

الباب الأول: الفصل الأول - تطوّر نظرية المعرفة
وهذا التصنيف للعناصر يعني فيما يعني أن التربية الإسلامية قائمة على الربط بين الفكر والسلوك، أو النظرية والتطبيق وفق هذا الترتيب المنطقي. ويتوسع أحد الباحثين المشتغلين بقضية أسلمة المعرفة في تصور هذه العناصر فيبلغ بها خمساً على النحو التالي:
١ - العقل السليم.
٢ - القرآن.
٣ - الكون.
٤ - الميراث الإنساني.
٥ - عملية هضم وتمثل لهذه العناصر (۱).
والواقع أن تصنيف العناصر على هذا النحو أقرب إلى المرادفة بين أغلبها وبين مصادر المعرفة وطرائقها كما هو واضح في العناصر الثلاثة الأولى. ولكن ذلك لا يغير من حقيقة الفلسفة العملية من حيث الاتفاق على ضرورة هضمها وتمثلها في الواقع الإنساني بصورة عامة والتربوي بوجه خاص.
ويكشف أحد الباحثين جميع تلك العناصر في مسألتين رئيستين هما: العلم والإيمان وما يتعلق بهما من لوازم عضوية تأتي على كل العناصر الفرعية التي سبق إبراز بعضها (٢).
(۱) التيجاني عبد القادر حامد مقدمة في تأصيل المعرفة، ٤٠٢.
(۲) انظر العلم والإيمان مدخل إلى نظرية المعرفة في الإسلام لإبراهيم أحمد عمر.
Chapter One: Section One - Development of Epistemology. This classification of elements means inter alia that Islamic education is based on linking thought and behavior, or theory and practice according to this logical order. One researcher working on the issue of Islamization of knowledge extends these elements to five as follows: 1 - Sound intellect. 2 - The Quran. 3 - The universe. 4 - Human heritage. 5 - Process of digestion and representation of these elements (1). In reality, the classification of elements in this manner is closer to synonymy between most of them and the sources and methods of knowledge, as is clear in the first three elements. But that does not change the fact of practical philosophy regarding the agreement on the necessity of digesting and representing them in human reality in general and educational reality in particular. One researcher reveals all those elements in two main issues: knowledge and faith and their organic necessities that encompass all the subsidiary elements previously highlighted (2). (1) Tijani Abd al-Qadir Hamid, Introduction to the Foundation of Knowledge, p. 402. (2) See: Knowledge and Faith: Introduction to the Theory of Knowledge in Islam by Ibrahim Ahmad Umar.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage introduces a classification of the elements of Islamic epistemology by a researcher working on Islamization of knowledge. The author begins by stating that this classification implies that Islamic education connects thought and behavior or theory and practice logically. The researcher expands the elements to five: sound intellect, the Quran, the universe, human heritage, and the process of digesting and representing these elements. The author then critiques this classification, noting that it is nearly synonymous with sources and methods of knowledge, especially the first three. However, this does not diminish the importance of practical philosophy, which requires internalizing these elements in human and educational reality. Finally, another researcher reduces all elements to two main issues: knowledge and faith, with their organic necessities covering all subsidiary elements.

Key Terms
العقل السليم
الميراث الإنساني
عملية هضم وتمثل

Key Takeaway
The five-element classification of Islamic epistemology, while practical, is logically redundant and can be reduced to knowledge and faith.

The Relationship Between Epistemology and Theory of Knowledge
Author clarifies the relationship between epistemology and theory of knowledge, distinguishing French and English meanings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the French and English meanings of 'epistemology' and explain which view the author adopts regarding its connection to theory of knowledge.

Core Idea
Epistemology and theory of knowledge are neither identical nor separate; their link depends on linguistic tradition.

The author has been discussing the nature of theory and knowledge in the Quran. Before moving forward, he clarifies how he understands the term 'epistemology' (الإبستمولوجيا) in relation to 'theory of knowledge' (نظرية المعرفة). This short but crucial passage sets the methodological foundation for the entire work. You need to grasp his distinction to follow his later arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rejected extremes
Locate the two positions the author dismisses: (1) completely detaching epistemology from theory of knowledge, and (2) restricting epistemology to philosophy of science. These are stated in the first sentence.
The author calls the first 'a remote doctrine' and the second 'something that will not remove us from confusion'.
2
Find the author's middle position
The author proposes that the most acceptable view is that there is 'a degree of connection and a degree of separation' between epistemology and theory of knowledge. This is his intermediate stance.
This applies within the French meaning of the term (as he clarifies later).
3
Contrast the French and English meanings
Under the French meaning, there is partial overlap; under the English meaning, epistemology is essentially synonymous with theory of knowledge. The author explicitly states this distinction.
The English meaning is 'more accurate from the standpoint of the universality of knowledge'.
4
Determine the author's preferred meaning
The author leans toward the more comprehensive English sense, as it better serves a global and civilizational perspective on knowledge. This is relevant to his project on Quranic theory.
This choice underlies his treatment of knowledge in the rest of the work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصفوة القول إزاء كل ما سبق: إن تجريد الإبستمولوجيا عن نظرية المعرفة بإطلاق مذهب بعيد، وحصر تفسير الإبستمولوجيا بفلسفة العلوم أمر لـن يخرجنا من الإشكال والغموض، وقد سبق القول بأن كل تفكير في أي علم أو في جانب من جوانبه إنما هو بصورة ما فلسفة لهذا العلم. ولذلك فإن الرأي القائل بوجود قدر من الاتصال وقدر من الانفصال بين المصطلحين هو الأقرب إلى القبول هذا في إطار المعنى الفرنسي للإبستمولوجيا. أما إذا نظرنا إلى الموضوع من منظور أكثر شمولية، وذلك حين نستصحب المعنى الإنجليزي للمصطلح، فإن القول بأن الإبستمولوجيا لا تخرج في معناها العام عن نظرية المعرفة يكون أكثر دقة من منطلق عالمية المعرفية، وتفاعلها الحضاري.
In summary of all that preceded: That detaching epistemology from theory of knowledge absolutely is a remote doctrine, and limiting the interpretation of epistemology to philosophy of science is something that will not remove us from confusion and ambiguity. And it has been said before that every thinking about any science or aspect of it is, in some way, a philosophy of that science. Therefore, the opinion that there is a degree of connection and a degree of separation between the two terms is the most acceptable, this within the French meaning of epistemology. But if we look at the subject from a more comprehensive perspective, when we adopt the English meaning of the term, then saying that epistemology does not go beyond its general meaning from theory of knowledge is more accurate from the standpoint of the universality of knowledge and its civilizational interaction.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a methodological clarification by the author. He summarizes his view on the relationship between epistemology and theory of knowledge, arguing against two extremes: completely detaching epistemology from theory of knowledge, or limiting epistemology to philosophy of science. He proposes a middle ground: there is partial connection and separation, especially in the French tradition. However, in the broader English sense, epistemology is essentially synonymous with theory of knowledge. This discussion sets the stage for defining 'theory' in the Quran.

Distinguishing Revelation from Human Theory
Author critiques the conflation of divine revelation with human interpretive theories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between divine revelation (wahy) and human theory (nazariyya/ijtihad) in Islamic scholarship, and explain why this distinction is crucial for proper ijtihad.

Core Idea
Revelation is absolute and infallible; human theory is relative and fallible – never confuse the two.

In this passage, the author takes aim at a common error: treating the results of human ijtihad as if they were on par with divine revelation. He argues that many researchers fail to separate the sacred, eternal texts from the fallible, time-bound understandings of scholars. This lesson will help you identify that confusion and understand why it matters for every Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of confusion
The author points out that researchers often conflate infallible revelation (wahy) with fallible ijtihad (nazariyya). Look for places where a scholar's interpretation is treated as having the same authority as the text itself.
This confusion arises when the human role in processing revelation is overlooked.
2
Distinguish the two concepts
Revelation (Qur'an and Sunnah) is sacred, absolute, eternal, and protected from error. Theory (nazariyya) is the researcher's understanding, subject to give-and-take, acceptance, rejection, and error.
The author equates nazariyya with ijtihad – both are products of human intellect interacting with the text.
3
Analyse the consequence of confusion
If we treat the meanings of revelation as fixed and unchangeable, we deny the Qur'an's eternity and universal applicability. The Qur'an would be exhausted by earlier understandings, contradicting its inimitability.
The author argues that relativity and probability attach to the human theorist, not to revelation itself.
4
Apply the principle to Islamic sciences
In any field (fiqh, tafsir, kalam), check whether a claim is directly from revelation or is a human inference. The latter is open to critique and revision; the former is not.
This tool protects the sanctity of revelation while allowing legitimate scholarly debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمعلوم أن نصوص السنة تشمل ما هو قطعي في الورود والدلالة أو ما هو ظنيها، والقرآن يشترك مع صحيح السنة في قدر لا يستهان بـه مـن النصوص ظنية الدلالة جميع ذلك مما لم يراعه الباحث، بل تجاوزه إلى تحميل دعاة بناء نظرية تربوية إسلامية)، الخلط في الينابيع بين الوحي المعصوم والاجتهاد القابل للنقد، العرضة للرد والخلط الحقيقي إنما هو في فهمه، إذ لم يفرق بين النظرية وبين مصادرها بحيث أغفل دور الإنسان في التعامل مع المصادر البلورة النظرية. ولعله من الطّريف هنا الإشارة إلى أن أحد الباحثين تلك عنه الذين أخذ عليهم الباحث وصفهم للتربية الإسلامية بالنظرية باحث عرف الالتزام بنصوص الوحي في كتاباته ومنهجه عموماً، وعُرف أيضاً بتشدده في استخدام بعض المصطلحات كوصف التربية الإسلامية بـ(الفلسفة) مثلاً، ومع ذلك فإن مأخذ الباحث - صاحب الرد - عليه كان في استخدامه (مصطلح النظرية لوصف التربية الإسلامية بها والسؤال إذن كيف يختلف باحث مسلم ينهل من معين نصوص الكتاب والسنة مع زميله الذي ينهل من المعين ذاته؟ الحق أن ذلك يعود - قبل أي سبب آخر - إلى عدم تحرير النزاع في مصطلحي الوحي والنظرية على نحو كاف. وإذا كنا قد عرفنا طبيعة نصوص الوحي فيما سبق فإن مصلح (نظرية) هو الآخر بحاجة إلى تحرير محل النزاع فيه. وفي سبيل هذا أقول: لعله من غير المقبول ولا المعقول أن يتبادر إلى الذهن أن باحثاً مسلماً ملتزماً - بالتربية الإسلامية أو سواها – لا يفرق عن قصد بين نصوص الكتاب وصحيح السنة وبين الاجتهاد الذي يساوي معنى النظرية بجامع الأخذ والعطاء، والقبول والرفض، واحتمال الوقوع في الخطأ أو الباطل كذلك. إن الاجتهاد أو النظرية – بحسب اصطلاح الدراسة – هو الذي يجري عليه كل تلك العوارض، أي إن الاجتهاد نتاج لتفاعل العقل مع النص، وليس مدخلاً مع النص ابتداء كمقدمة له تتساوى في نتيجتها مع مراد النص تماماً. وبتعبير آخر أكثر تحديداً فإن النظرية المقصودة هنا هي نظرية الباحث أو نظرته إلى مدلولات الوحي كيما تتشكل هذه النظرية لبلورتها في أي ميدان، ومنها ميدان التربية. والباحث - أي باحث - إذ يسعى لصناعة هذه النظرية إنما ينطلق في آفاق النصوص الظنية الدلالة، والتي تشكل معظم الوحي. ولو أن مدلولات النصوص القرآنية والنبوية حملت على معنى واحد لا يتغير بتغير الأزمة والأمكنة والأحوال والعوائد بدعوى أنها جميعاً نصوص مستقاة من الوحي ؛ إذن لم يكن معنی لخلود القرآن وإعجازه وكونه خطاباً عالمياً مطلقاً، يتجاوز حدود الزمان والمكان، ويصلح لكل الظروف، وينهل كل باحث منه كليات وأصولاً في تخصصه إذ يصبح - والحال هكذا - قد استنفد أغراضه في فهـوم السابقين، الذين ربما أتوا على كل آية بياناً وتفسيراً وفق معطياتهم المعرفية المحكومة يومذاك بالظروف الموضوعية، تلك التي تحكم حركة المعرفة بصورة عامة. ولكن أحداً منهم لم يدع أن القرآن قد توقف عطاؤه في الفهم والاستنباط عنده أو في زمن معاصريه. ومن هنا فإن النسبية والظن وكل ما يجري على الباحث من عوارض إنسانية إنما تلحق صاحب النظرية لا الوحي ذاته، إذ الوحي مقدس مصون ومطلق خالد. أوليس ذلك هو أدب التعامل مع القرآن الكريم والسنة المطهرة بدلاً من ادعاء الوصاية فيهما، أو النطق باسم الوحي، أو الخلط بين النص الإلهي المطلق الخالد، والفهم الإنساني المظنون النسبي؟
It is known that the texts of the Sunnah include what is definitive in transmission and meaning or what is probable in them, and the Qur'an shares with the authentic Sunnah a considerable amount of texts that are probable in meaning. All of this is not taken into account by the researcher, rather he exceeds it to burden the advocates of building an Islamic educational theory with confusion in the sources between infallible revelation and ijtihad that is open to criticism, subject to refutation. The real confusion is only in his understanding, for he did not distinguish between the theory and its sources, neglecting the role of the human being in dealing with the sources for developing the theory. It might be interesting here to point out that one of the researchers whom the researcher criticized for describing Islamic education as a theory—a researcher known for commitment to the texts of revelation in his writings and methodology in general, and also known for his strictness in using some terms like describing Islamic education as 'philosophy', for example—nevertheless, the point of criticism of the researcher (the author of the refutation) against him was his use of the term 'theory' to describe Islamic education. The question then is: how does a Muslim researcher who draws from the same source of the Book and Sunnah differ from his colleague who draws from the same source? The truth is that this is due—before any other reason—to insufficient clarification of the dispute concerning the terms 'revelation' and 'theory'. And if we have known the nature of the texts of revelation previously, then the term 'theory' also needs clarification of the point of dispute. Toward this end, I say: It is neither acceptable nor reasonable to think that a committed Muslim researcher—in Islamic education or otherwise—does not deliberately distinguish between the texts of the Book and authentic Sunnah on one hand, and ijtihad which is equivalent to the meaning of theory, in terms of give and take, acceptance and rejection, and the possibility of falling into error or falsehood. Indeed, ijtihad or theory—according to the terminology of the study—is that which is subject to all those contingencies, meaning that ijtihad is the product of the interaction of the intellect with the text, and not an entry alongside the text from the beginning as a premise that equals the intended meaning of the text completely. In other words, more specifically, the theory intended here is the researcher's theory or his view of the implications of revelation, so that this theory forms for its crystallization in any field, including the field of education. And the researcher—any researcher—when he seeks to construct this theory, he launches into the horizons of the texts of probable meaning, which constitute most of revelation. If the meanings of the Qur'anic and Prophetic texts were taken as a single meaning that does not change with changing times, places, circumstances, and customs, under the pretext that they are all texts derived from revelation, then there would be no meaning to the eternity of the Qur'an, its inimitability, and its being an absolute universal discourse that transcends the boundaries of time and place, suitable for all circumstances, and every researcher draws from it general principles and foundations in his specialty, because it would then—in such a case—have exhausted its purposes in the understandings of the predecessors, who perhaps provided full explanation and interpretation of every verse according to their cognitive givens, at that time governed by objective circumstances that control the movement of knowledge in general. But none of them claimed that the Qur'an had stopped its contribution in understanding and deduction in their time or the time of their contemporaries. Hence, relativity, probability, and all the human contingencies that afflict the researcher only attach to the author of the theory, not to revelation itself, for revelation is sacred, protected, absolute, and eternal. Is that not the proper etiquette of dealing with the Noble Qur'an and the Purified Sunnah, instead of claiming guardianship over them, or speaking in the name of revelation, or confusing the absolute eternal divine text with the probable relative human understanding?
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage critiques a common confusion among researchers who conflate divine revelation with human theoretical constructs. The author begins by reminding that the texts of the Sunnah—and similarly the Qur'an—include both definitive and probable aspects. Many researchers fail to distinguish between infallible revelation and fallible ijtihad (interpretive effort). The real confusion lies in not differentiating between a theory and its sources, and overlooking the human role in processing those sources to form a theory. The author then illustrates this with an example of a researcher who criticized another for using the term 'theory' for Islamic education, despite being himself committed to revelation. The key point is that two Muslim researchers drawing from the same sources can differ precisely because they have not sufficiently clarified the terms 'revelation' and 'theory'. The author insists that no committed Muslim would intentionally equate the texts of revelation with ijtihad, which shares attributes of acceptance and rejection, and is prone to error. Ijtihad or theory is the product of the intellect interacting with the text, not a co-equal entry alongside the text. The theory in question is the researcher's own understanding of the implications of revelation. The author then makes a striking argument: if the meanings of revealed texts were fixed and unchangeable, then the Qur'an would cease to be eternal, inimitable, and universally applicable. Instead, the Qur'an continues to yield new understandings, and no early scholar claimed it was exhausted. Therefore, relativity and probability pertain only to the human theorist, not to revelation itself. The passage concludes with a call to proper adab (etiquette) toward the Qur'an and Sunnah: not to claim guardianship, speak in their name, or confuse the absolute divine text with relative human understanding.

Key Terms
نظرية
اجتهاد
وحي

Is Islam a Theory? Analyzing the Critique
Author poses and defends the application of 'theory' to Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the author's argument for calling Islam a theory and critically assess the grounds of his rejection of the opposing view.

Core Idea
Denying Islam the status of theory reveals conceptual confusion, not scholarly rigor.

The author raises a provocative question: can the comprehensive system of Islam be described as a 'theory'? He expresses astonishment at those who deny it with hesitation. This lesson unpacks his critique and examines its methodological foundations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and the target
What is the author asserting about Islam and the term 'nazariyya'? Who is he criticizing? The passage states that after establishing basic concepts, it is valid to ask whether Islam can be called a theory. He criticizes those who answer negatively with hesitation and confusion.
2
Extract the grounds of his astonishment
Why does the author find the denial strange? He describes the denial as 'accompanied by a degree of hesitation and confusion', which he finds astonishing and objectionable. He implies that the denial is unnecessary.
3
Analyze the presuppositions
What assumptions about 'theory' does the author hold? The author assumes that Islam has systematic concepts and postulates that aim to be realized in man and society, thus qualifying as a theory. His critique presupposes that a theory is a coherent framework with practical goals.
4
Evaluate the critique's logic
Is the author's objection logically sound? The critique is more rhetorical than logical; it expresses disapproval but does not provide a rigorous argument for why Islam must be called a theory. The validity depends on the definition of 'theory' assumed.
Consider how a definition of 'nazariyya' in Islamic thought might differ from modern Western notions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المفاهيم والمسلمات الأساسية. فغاية النظرية التربوية في الإسلام هي تحقيق هذه المفاهيم والمسلمات والإجابات الكبرى في الإنسان والمجتمع))) أبعد ذلك يصح أن يطرح هذا التساؤل: هل يصح لنا أن نطلق على الإسلام مصطلح نظرية ..؟ وأغرب منه أن يجيب بالنفي المصحوب بقدر من التلكؤ والاضطراب (۲)، مما يبعث على الاستغراب والاستنكار معاً، وقد كان في غنى عن ذلك كله.
Basic concepts and postulates. The goal of educational theory in Islam is to realize these concepts, postulates, and major answers in man and society. After that, it is valid to raise this question: Is it correct for us to apply the term 'theory' to Islam? And what is stranger is that some answer in the negative, accompanied by a degree of hesitation and confusion, which together evokes astonishment and disapproval, while he could have done without all that.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary. The author begins by stating that the goal of Islamic educational theory is to realize basic concepts and postulates. He then poses the question: can Islam be termed a 'theory'? He criticizes those who answer negatively, describing their response as hesitant and confused, and finds it astonishing and objectionable. The author implies that denying Islam the status of a theory is unnecessary and misguided. The tone is rhetorical rather than argumentative, serving as a prelude to a more detailed discussion of definitions.

Key Terms
نظرية (nazariyya): A systematic framework or doctrine that explains phenomena; here applied to Islam as a comprehensive worldview. [Note: In Islamic thought, nazariyya often contrasts with 'amaliyya (practical); in modern contexts it may carry Western philosophical connotations.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) They propose a different terminology.

Key Takeaway
The author argues that denying Islam the label of 'theory' is unnecessary and reflects conceptual confusion about the nature of theoretical frameworks in Islamic thought.

Balance Between Subjective and Objective Knowledge in Islamic Education
Discusses the balance between subjective and objective views of knowledge in education.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the extremes of subjective and objective knowledge and explain the Islamic principle of balance in educational epistemology.

Core Idea
Neither pure subjectivity nor objectivity suffices; Islamic education balances both.

This passage from a modern educational text discusses the tension between subjective and objective views of knowledge. It warns against extremes and advocates a balanced approach that considers both the learner's internal development and the external reality of the subject matter. The principle of balance (tawazun) is deeply rooted in Islamic thought, from fiqh to kalam, and is essential for sound pedagogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two extremes
Locate where the passage describes the consequences of purely subjective and purely objective knowledge. Note the claims that if knowledge is completely subjective, teaching cannot occur; if completely objective, the learner must conform to external reality.
The passage mentions both extremes explicitly.
2
Extract the balance principle
Find the sentence that states the Islamic educational principle requires attention to both learner and subject matter. This is the balanced approach.
The phrase 'مبدأ التوازن في التربية الإسلامية يقتضي الاهتمام بالأمرين معا' is key.
3
Relate to classical 'ilm
Compare the passage's dichotomy with classical Islamic epistemology. In the Islamic tradition, 'ilm is both objective (haqīqa, corresponding to reality) and subjective (ma'rifa, involving personal understanding and faith). Consider how the Ash'ari position balances divine revelation and human reason.
This step bridges the modern text to classical concepts.
4
Apply to an educational scenario
Think of a concrete example from Islamic education, such as teaching the Quran. The objective aspect is the revealed text itself; the subjective aspect is the student's interpretation and connection. The balanced approach would respect both the integrity of the text and the learner's context.
Apply the principle to avoid extremes: neither rigid memorization without understanding nor purely subjective interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني - تمهيد هذا التعريف من الزاوية التربوية تركيز الاهتمام على المتعلم والمادة معا، درعا للتطرف الذي يركز الاهتمام كله على المتعلم، حين الأخذ بالاتجاه القائل بذاتية المعرفة. وبالمقابل فإن هناك من يرى موضوعية المعرفة، وذلك يعني انصراف الاهتمام إلى المادة الدراسية. ومبدأ التوازن في التربية الإسلامية يقتضي الاهتمام بالأمرين معا. ويزيد فينكس الأمر تفصيلاً فيقول: ...... فإذا كانت المعرفة موضوعية تماما فإن المتعلم يتضمن الامتثال لما يوجد في الخارج. والعقل على هذا الأساس يجب أن يطبع على الدوام على نمو طبيعة الأشياء الخارجية. فالتدريب والتركيز على المعلومات المعروفة، والملاحظة الدقيقة للحقائق هي بعض طرق تشكيل الفهم حتى يتفق مع ما هو موجود موضوعيًا. وإذا كانت المعرفة ذاتية تماما فإن التدريس لا يمكن أن يحدث بأي حال من الأحوال. فالنمو يجب أن يحدث من الداخل عن طريق القوانين الداخلة في تكوين الفرد. وإذا نظرنا إلى المعرفة على أن لها مكونات ذاتية وأخرى موضوعية منفصلة أو متصلة، فإن التوجيه التعليمي سيحدث مع اهتمام بطبيعة العالم الخارجي، واهتمام بالقوى الداخلية كالمشاعر والأهداف والنظرات التي تكون شروط المعرفة. فالإدراك والفهم لن يدخلا في تشكيلات مقننة لحقيقة لا يمكن تغييرها، كما يقال، ولن يسمح لها بحرية التفضيل الخاص حُرّية لا تناقش. ولكنها ستشتق الكشف الجالة للعالم وتراجع على أساسه. وبهذا توضّح فضل العناصر الخاصة - الفردية والجماعية – التي تتضمنها كل معرفة، ذات مغزى وارتباط إنساني.
Chapter Two - Introduction to this definition from an educational perspective: focusing attention on both the learner and the subject matter, as a shield against extremism that focuses all attention on the learner, when adopting the view that knowledge is subjective. Conversely, there are those who see knowledge as objective, meaning that attention is directed to the subject matter. And the principle of balance in Islamic education requires attention to both. Phenix adds detail, saying: ...... If knowledge is completely objective, then the learner involves compliance with what exists in the outside. The mind, on this basis, must constantly be imprinted on the growth of the nature of external things. Training and concentration on known information, and careful observation of facts, are some ways of shaping understanding so that it agrees with what exists objectively. And if knowledge is completely subjective, then teaching cannot occur under any circumstances. Growth must occur from within through the laws internal to the formation of the individual. And if we look at knowledge as having subjective and objective components, separate or connected, then educational guidance will occur with attention to the nature of the external world, and attention to internal forces such as feelings, goals, and perspectives that constitute the conditions of knowledge. Perception and understanding will not enter into codified formations of an unchangeable truth, as it is said, nor will they be allowed the freedom of personal preference, an undiscussed freedom. Rather, they will derive the revelation [or discovery] of the world and revise it on that basis. And by this, the virtue of the special elements - individual and collective - that every knowledge contains, having meaning and human connection, becomes clear.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage discusses the epistemological foundation of education, focusing on two competing views of knowledge: subjective and objective. The author begins by stating that an educational definition should balance attention between the learner and the subject matter, as a safeguard against extremism that overemphasizes the learner when adopting the subjective view. In contrast, the objective view shifts all attention to the subject matter. Islamic education, with its principle of balance, requires attention to both. The author then cites Phenix to elaborate: If knowledge is completely objective, the learner must conform to external reality, and the mind is shaped through training, concentration, and observation to match objective facts. If knowledge is completely subjective, teaching becomes impossible because growth must come from within through internal laws. A middle perspective recognizes both subjective and objective components, leading to educational guidance that considers both external reality and internal factors like feelings and goals. Perception and understanding are not rigidly determined but are open to revision based on discovery. The passage concludes that such a view highlights the special individual and collective elements inherent in all meaningful, humanly connected knowledge.

Key Terms
معرفة ذاتية (ma'rifa dhātiyya) - subjective knowledge
معرفة موضوعية (ma'rifa mawḍū'iyya) - objective knowledge

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Teaching becomes highly effective by focusing on the learner's internal growth.
B) Teaching cannot occur at all because growth must come from within.
C) The learner must conform to external reality.
D) The subject matter becomes irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
Islamic education rejects extremes and requires a balanced integration of objective reality and subjective learner engagement.

The Quranic Call to Verification
Author explains Quranic prohibition of speaking without knowledge and need for verification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Quranic basis for requiring verification (tahqeeq) in acquiring knowledge and distinguish between valid and invalid grounds for knowledge claims.

Core Idea
The Quran commands verification, not blind acceptance.

This passage establishes a foundational principle of Islamic epistemology: knowledge claims must be verified through the senses, reason, and the heart, not merely transmitted. A single verse from Surat al-Isra' is used to derive this principle, which has profound implications for how we receive and transmit knowledge in all Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Verse and Its Context
Locate the Quranic verse (17:36) in the passage. Note the faculties mentioned: hearing, sight, and the heart. The verse forbids pursuing what you have no knowledge of.
The heart (fu'ad) here refers to the intellect or inner perception.
2
Extract the Prohibition
The author says the Quran prohibits 'delving into what sensory and rational methods cannot ascertain.' This means one should not make claims that cannot be supported by evidence from the senses or reason.
This excludes matters beyond human capacity, but within our scope, we must rely on evidence.
3
Derive the Positive Requirement
From the prohibition, the author derives two positive injunctions: deliberation (al-ta'anni) and verification (tahqeeq). Knowledge must be actively checked, not passively received.
Contrast this with mere transmission (naql) or blind following (taqlid).
4
Apply to Islamic Sciences
Consider how this principle operates in kalam, usul al-fiqh, and hadith. For example, in evaluating reports for aqida, scholars require tawatur or strong evidence, rejecting weak isolated reports.
Without this tool, unverified claims could corrupt belief and practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد شدّد القرآن الكريم في النهي عن الخوض فيما لم تتمكن طرائق المعرفة الحسية والعقلية من الوقوف عنده: ﴿وَلا تَقْفُ مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْمٌ إِنَّ السَّمْعَ وَالْبَصَرَ وَالْفُؤادَ كُلُّ أُولَئِكَ كانَ عَنْهُ مَسْؤُولاً [الإسراء: ٣٦/١٧]. وهذا يفيد ضرورة التأني في تلقي المعرفة، وعدم جوار التسرع في الحكم، أي إنه يعني تحقيق المعرفة، وعدم الاكتفاء بالنقل للمعرفة عن الآخرين فحسب.
And the Noble Quran emphasized the prohibition of delving into what the sensory and rational methods of knowledge have not been able to ascertain: {And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge. Indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart - all of those will be questioned.} [Al-Isra' 17:36]. And this indicates the necessity of deliberation in receiving knowledge, and the impermissibility of haste in judgment, i.e., it means verifying knowledge, and not merely being satisfied with transmitting knowledge from others.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage cites Quranic authority for the principle of scientific methodology. The author first states that the Quran strongly prohibits engaging in matters that cannot be accessed by sensory or rational means. He then quotes the verse from Surat al-Isra' which commands not to follow what one has no knowledge of, and reminds that the faculties of hearing, sight, and heart will be held accountable. The explanation following the verse extracts two implications: first, the need for deliberation (al-ta'anni) when receiving knowledge; second, the prohibition of rushing to judgment. In effect, this means that knowledge must be verified (tahqeeq) and not merely transmitted from others. This principle is fundamental in Islamic epistemology, where hearsay (taqlid) is not sufficient for certain knowledge in matters of belief and important rulings.

Key Terms
المنهج العلمي
التأني

D) That we should accept all transmitted knowledge as true.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic imperative to verify knowledge before accepting or transmitting it is a cornerstone of Islamic scientific methodology.

Intellectual Trust: Attributing Knowledge to Its Sources
Author discusses trustworthiness in knowledge transmission and attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Islamic principle of amana applies to intellectual property and knowledge attribution, and identify the Quranic basis for this obligation.

Core Idea
Attributing knowledge to its source is a sacred trust, not just an academic courtesy.

This passage connects a general Islamic value—trustworthiness—to the specific duty of proper attribution in scholarship. The author argues that just as we must return physical objects to their owners, we must return ideas to their originators. This lesson helps you see the Quranic foundation for academic integrity.

Guided Path
1
Define the general concept of amana
Read the passage and identify what the author says about trustworthiness. Note that it is a broad Islamic principle covering all areas of life.
The author mentions 'amana' as a general concept before narrowing to intellectual trusts.
2
Distinguish physical and intellectual trusts
The author explicitly contrasts physical trusts (e.g., property) with intellectual trusts (knowledge, ideas). List the specific forms of intellectual betrayal mentioned: plagiarism, falsification, distortion.
The Arabic terms are 'intihal' (plagiarism), 'tazyif' (falsification), 'tahwir' (distortion).
3
Examine the first Quranic citation (4:58)
Verse 4:58 commands rendering trusts to their owners. How does this apply to knowledge? The author uses it as a general principle that includes intellectual content.
4
Examine the second Quranic citation (8:27)
Verse 8:27 prohibits betraying Allah, the Messenger, and one's trusts knowingly. How does this escalate the severity? The author emphasizes that such betrayal is especially grave when committed with awareness.
5
Synthesize the prohibition
The passage concludes that failing to attribute knowledge properly contradicts the Quranic commands and is a clear violation. Explain in your own words why accurate attribution is a religious duty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كان مفهوم الأمانة عاماً واسعاً، فإن من أولويات ما يندرج تحته بعد الأمانات الحسية، أمانة النقل والتوثيق وعزو المعارف بما فيها من أفكار وفهومات وقيم إلى أصحابها من غير ادعاء أو انتحال، أو تزييف، أو تحوير ... إلخ إذ إن هذا يتنافى ومفهوم أداء الأمانات إلى أهلها: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَأْمُرُكُمْ أَن تُؤَدُّوا الأماناتِ إِلَى أَهْلِهَا﴾ [النساء: ٥٨/٤]. ويوقع صاحبه في المخالفة الصريحة لنهي الله تعالى عن خيانة الأمانة خاصة حين تكون على علم: ﴿ويا أيها الذينَ آمَنُوا لا تَخُونُوا اللهَ وَالرَّسُولَ وَتَخُونُوا أَمَانَاتِكُمْ وَأَنتُمْ تَعْلَمُونَ [الأنفال: ۲۷/۸].
And if the concept of trustworthiness is general and broad, then among the priorities of what falls under it, after physical trusts, is the trustworthiness of transmission, documentation, and attribution of knowledge, including its ideas, understandings, and values, to their owners, without claiming, plagiarism, falsification, or distortion... etc. Indeed, this contradicts the concept of rendering trusts to their owners: {Indeed, Allah commands you to render trusts to their owners} [An-Nisa' 4:58]. And it lands its doer in clear violation of Allah's prohibition of betraying trust, especially when done knowingly: {O you who have believed, do not betray Allah and the Messenger or betray your trusts while you know} [Al-Anfal 8:27].
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage applies the general Islamic principle of 'amana (trustworthiness) to the realm of knowledge. The author distinguishes between physical trusts (e.g., property) and intellectual trusts. The latter include the obligation to properly transmit, document, and attribute ideas, understandings, and values to their original authors. Any form of plagiarism (intihal), falsification (tazyif), or distortion (tahwir) is a breach of this trust. Two Quranic verses are cited: first, the command to render trusts to their owners (4:58), which is a general principle; second, the prohibition of betraying Allah, His Messenger, and one's trusts knowingly (8:27). The author emphasizes that such betrayal is especially severe when done with knowledge. This lesson reinforces academic integrity as a religious duty.

Key Terms
أمانة النقل والتوثيق
انتحال
تزييف
تحوير
أمانة

Key Takeaway
Trustworthiness in knowledge requires accurate attribution to original sources, as commanded by the Quran and emphasized by the prohibition of betraying trusts.

The Prohibition of Fabricating Rulings: Halal and Haram Belong to Allah Alone
Author warns against falsely declaring things halal or haram without divine authority, citing Quran 16:116.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the exclusive right of Allah in determining halal and haram and explain why fabricating rulings is epistemologically invalid.

Core Idea
The authority to declare halal and haram belongs exclusively to Allah; any claim without divine authorization is fabrication.

In this passage, the author warns against the grave sin of issuing rulings on halal and haram based on personal motives or dishonesty. He grounds this prohibition in the Quranic injunction from Surah an-Nahl, connecting it to the concept of rabbaniyya (divine-orientedness). As students of Islamic knowledge, you must internalize that the source of legislative authority is Allah alone, and any attempt to bypass this is a form of lying against Allah. This lesson will equip you with the epistemological framework to distinguish between legitimate rulings rooted in revelation and fabricated ones driven by desire.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the claim
Identify the central claim: no one has the right to determine halal and haram except Allah. The author states this directly and backs it with Quranic evidence.
2
Locate the evidence
Find the Quranic verse cited (16:116). Explain how the verse explicitly forbids falsely labeling things as halal or haram and equates it to lying against Allah.
3
Understand the consequence
What does the author say about the motive behind such fabrications? He mentions 'insincere motive' (dāfiʿ ghayr nazīh). This shows that even good intentions do not justify issuing rulings without divine authority.
4
Connect to broader concept
How does the author link this to rabbaniyya? Rabbaniyya means being grounded in divine revelation. Islamic education must be characterized by this orientation; otherwise, knowledge becomes detached from its source and leads to falsehood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذلك أن ليس من حق أحد تقرير الموضوعات التشريعية لإصدار أحكام الحل والحرمة بدافع غير نزيه هو دافع الافتراء والكذب؛ لأن التحليل والتحريم حق الله - تعالى - وحده: ﴿وَلا تَقُولُوا لِما تَصِفُ أَلْسِنَتُكُمُ الْكَذِبَ هَذا حَلالٌ وَهَذَا حَرَامٌ لِتَفْتَرُوا عَلَى اللَّهِ الْكَذِبَ ﴾ [النحل: ١١٦/١٦]. وهذا يندرج تحت سمة الربانية التي تتصف بها التربية الإسلامية وقد أشرنا إلى ذلك قبلاً.
And that is because no one has the right to determine legislative matters to issue rulings of permissibility and prohibition with an insincere motive, that of fabrication and lies. Because analysis and prohibition are the exclusive right of Allah, the Exalted. {And do not say about what your tongues assert of falsehood, 'This is lawful and this is unlawful,' to invent falsehood about Allah} [An-Nahl 16:116]. And this falls under the characteristic of divine-orientedness (rabbaniyya) that characterizes Islamic education, and we have referred to that previously.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage addresses the grave sin of issuing religious rulings without divine authorization. The author states that no one has the right to declare things halal or haram based on dishonest motives such as fabrication and lying. The authority to determine what is lawful and unlawful belongs exclusively to Allah. The Quranic verse from Surat an-Nahl (16:116) explicitly forbids people from falsely labeling things as halal or haram as a form of lying against Allah. The author then connects this to the concept of rabbaniyya (divine-orientedness), which is a core characteristic of Islamic education. This underscores that all knowledge, especially rulings, must be rooted in divine revelation, not personal whims or societal pressures.

Key Takeaway

The Challenge of Western Liberalism and the Quest for Unity of Knowledge
Author identifies challenges and lists institutional responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main reasons why Western liberalism was harder to resist than Marxism, and list at least three institutional signs of hope for unity of knowledge mentioned in the passage.

Core Idea
Unity of knowledge requires replacing dualistic education with an integrated Islamic framework.

Western liberalism posed a deeper challenge to Islamic education than Marxism because it permeated all branches of knowledge and Muslim scholars struggled to produce alternative Islamic concepts. The author points to earlier failed attempts at Islamizing curricula and then highlights promising institutions that are based on the principle of unity of knowledge, integrating revelation and science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two reasons for liberalism's resilience
Read the lines after 'لسببين رئيسين' (two main reasons). The author gives two: the influence of Western education on all fields, and the inability of Muslim scholars to formulate Islamic alternatives to liberal concepts.
These reasons explain why Marxism was easier to resist doctrinally.
2
Note the failure of early Islamization efforts
The passage states that earlier attempts to merge religious and secular education under 'Islamization of the curriculum' failed because they were one-sided and did not address the problem's complexity.
This sets up the need for a more comprehensive approach.
3
Extract the four signs of hope
The author lists four positive developments: (1) establishment of educational institutions based on unity of knowledge, (2) Yemen's educational philosophy based on tawhid and sharia, (3) Sudan's philosophy rejecting dualism and creating a 'Department of Rooting', (4) Islamic universities and intellectual institutes focused on Islamization.
These are not exhaustive but illustrative.
4
Understand the concept of unity of knowledge
The recurring theme is 'wahdat al-ma'rifa' – that revealed knowledge and cosmic (scientific) knowledge are not separate. Institutions that embody this reject artificial dualism (al-thuna'iyya al-mufta'ala) between religious and secular education.
This is the epistemological foundation of the reform movement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: الفصل الأول- أخلاق المعرفة ووحدتها
وكان من اليسير من وجهة النظر العقائدية البحتة مقاومة الأفكار الماركسية المهيمنة وقتذاك، ولكن كان من الصعوبة بمكان مقاومة آثار الليبرالية الغربية، وذلك لسببين رئيسين:
أحدهما : تأثير التربية الغربية على شتى فروع المعرفة.
ثانيهما: عدم تمكن علماء المسلمين من صياغة المفهومات الإسلامية التي يمكن لها أن تحل محل مثيلاتها الليبرالية (۱).
ومع أن جهودًا بُذلت في سبيل دمج نظامي التعليم الديني والعلماني في نظام واحد من منطلق فكرة أسلمة المنهاج إلا أنه لم يكتب لها النجاح، لأن معالجتها تميزت بالأحادية، ولم تلتفت إلى أبعاد المشكلة وجوانبها المختلفة (٢).
وعلى الرغم مما قد يبدو أنه استقصاء للمشكلة يشير إلى استعصاء الجوانبها يوما بعد آخر؛ إلا أنَّ ثمة مبشرات تفيد بأن ذلك الوضع لن يستمر طويلاً - بإذن الله تعالى - بالاستناد إلى جملة من المعطيات وأبرزها ما يلي:

أ - الإيمان بالله ووحدانيته خلق الكون وسخره للإنسان، وفق سنن إلهية دقيقة وثابتة.
(۱) المرجع السابق، ١٣ - ١٤.
(٢) المرجع نفسه، ٣٦.
ب - الإيمان بالإسلام عقيدة وشريعة ونظاماً شاملاً ينظم شؤون الحياة، ويكرم الإنسان، ويحترم عقله ودوره، ويتوافق مع فطرته، ويدعو إلى العلم والخلق والإبداع.
والقرآن الكريم والسنة النبوية الصحيحة يمثلان المنبع الروحي، والمرجع التشريعي الأول، وهما المصدران الأساسيان للنظرية التربوية بكل عناصرها))(۱).
٢ - فلسفة التربية في جمهورية السودان، التي أصبحت تقوم على أساس وحدة المعرفة وتكاملها ورفض الثنائية المفتعلة بين التعليم الديني والمدني. و من أجل تأصيل ذلك وتوطيده أنشأت وزارة التربية والتعليم إدارة مختصة لهذا الغرض أطلقت عليها إدارة التأصيل(٢).
- إنشاء جامعات إسلامية كبرى لا تقتصر على تبني هذا المفهوم التوحيدي في ذاتها فحسب، ولكنها تعمل على دراسته وتدريسه والسعي نحو استبداله بالأنظمة الثنائية المستوردة ويمكن ذكر الجامعة الإسلامية العالمية بكو للامبور في ماليزيا وجامعة العلوم الإسلامية والاجتماعية في ليزبرج بأمريكا.
٤- تأسيس معاهد فكرية تُعنى بإصلاح مناهج الفكر، ومن ضمنها مشكل الثنائية التعليمية هذه كما وتمثل روافد فكرية لتلك المؤسسات التربوية القائمة على أساس وحدة المعرفة، حيث تعنى بإسلامية المعرفة وتأصيلها، بما في ذلك
(۱) وزارة التربية والتعليم باليمن، القانون العام للتربية والتعليم الباب الثاني: الأسس والمبادئ العامة والأهداف.
(۲) انظر: العدد الأول من مجلة التأصيل التي تصدرها إدارة تأصيل المعرفة بوزارة التربية والتعليم والبحث العلمي بالسودان، وتأكيد الوزير هناك في ذلك الحين البروفيسور إبراهيم أحمد عمر على اعتماد الوحي مصدرًا للمعرفة إلى جانب المصادر الأخرى في مدارس وجامعات السودان: مقالة: إقامة الدين: التربية والتعليم والبحث العلمي، ص۱۰.
Chapter Two: First Section – The Ethics of Knowledge and Its Unity. It was easy from a purely doctrinal perspective to resist the dominant Marxist ideas at the time, but it was extremely difficult to resist the effects of Western liberalism, for two main reasons: First: the influence of Western education on all branches of knowledge. Second: the inability of Muslim scholars to formulate Islamic concepts that could replace their liberal counterparts (1). And although efforts were made to integrate the two systems of religious and secular education into one system based on the idea of Islamization of the curriculum, they were not successful because their approach was one-sided and did not attend to the dimensions and various aspects of the problem (2). Despite what may appear to be a comprehensive investigation of the problem indicating that its aspects are becoming more intractable day by day, there are positive signs that this situation will not last long – by the permission of Allah – based on a number of givens, the most prominent of which are the following: First: The establishment of educational, instructional, and higher academic institutions inside and outside the Muslim world, based on faith in the unity of knowledge and non-recourse to separating revelatory knowledge from cosmic knowledge. Among those institutions worth mentioning here – even if not all of them are adopted by the political systems of those countries, or there is another kind of separation between theory and practice – are the following: 1. The philosophy of education in the Republic of Yemen, which is based on: a. Faith in Allah and His oneness, His creation of the universe and subjugation of it to man, according to precise and constant divine laws. (1) Previous reference, pp. 13-14. (2) Same reference, p. 36. b. Faith in Islam as a creed, law, and comprehensive system that organizes the affairs of life, honors man, respects his intellect and role, is compatible with his innate nature, and calls for knowledge, creation, and innovation. The Noble Quran and the authentic Prophetic Sunnah represent the spiritual source and the first legislative reference, and they are the two primary sources of the educational theory with all its elements (1). 2. The philosophy of education in the Republic of Sudan, which has come to be based on the unity and integration of knowledge and the rejection of the artificial dualism between religious and civil education. In order to root and consolidate this, the Ministry of Education established a department specialized for this purpose, which it called the Department of Rooting (2). - The establishment of major Islamic universities that not only adopt this monotheistic concept within themselves, but also work to study it, teach it, and strive to replace the imported dual systems. One can mention the International Islamic University in Kuala Lumpur, Malaysia, and the University of Islamic and Social Sciences in Leesburg, USA. 4. The establishment of intellectual institutes concerned with reforming intellectual curricula, including this problem of educational dualism, and they represent intellectual tributaries for those educational institutions based on the unity of knowledge, being concerned with the Islamization of knowledge and its rooting, including (1) Ministry of Education in Yemen, General Law of Education, Chapter Two: General Foundations, Principles, and Objectives. (2) See: The first issue of Al-Ta'seel magazine, published by the Department of Rooting of Knowledge, Ministry of Education and Scientific Research in Sudan, and the emphasis of the then Minister, Professor Ibrahim Ahmed Omar, on adopting revelation as a source of knowledge alongside other sources in Sudan's schools and universities: Article: Establishing Religion: Education and Scientific Research, p. 10.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage discusses the challenge of Western liberal influence on Islamic education and the efforts to establish a unified knowledge system. The author begins by contrasting the ease of resisting Marxist ideas with the difficulty of resisting Western liberalism, attributing this to the pervasive influence of Western education and the inability of Muslim scholars to produce viable Islamic alternatives. The author notes that earlier attempts at Islamizing curricula failed due to a one-sided approach that ignored the problem's complexity. However, signs of hope are identified, primarily the establishment of educational institutions based on the unity of knowledge, avoiding separation between revealed and cosmic knowledge. The passage then lists specific examples: Yemen's educational philosophy based on faith in God and Islam; Sudan's philosophy rejecting dualism and creating a 'Department of Rooting'; Islamic universities like the International Islamic University Malaysia; and intellectual institutes focusing on Islamization of knowledge. The author concludes with references to official documents and publications.

Introduces the International Institute of Islamic Thought and its educational project.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key elements of the educational project of the International Institute of Islamic Thought (IIIT), including cognitive unity (wahdat al-ma'rifa) and Islamization (aslama).

Core Idea
Cognitive unity is the foundation for an Islamic educational curriculum.

This lesson introduces the International Institute of Islamic Thought (IIIT) as a contemporary initiative to integrate Islamic and modern knowledge. You will learn about its organizational structure and the key concepts of cognitive unity and Islamization that drive its educational project.

Guided Path

3

Maslow's Integration of Science and Religion: Why Religious Questions Matter
Presents Abraham Maslow's view that science must consider religious questions to avoid repeating past mistakes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Maslow's argument that science must respect religious questions and explain why he considers ignoring them pathological.

Core Idea
Science and religion are not separate worlds; ignoring religious questions is scientifically and psychologically unhealthy.

This passage introduces Abraham Maslow's call to expand the concept of science to include religious questions. He argues that the 19th-century atheist's mistake was to discard both questions and answers, and that modern scientists must engage with inquiries about origin, existence, and destiny. Maslow goes so far as to say that psychologists now view indifference to religion as abnormal. Understanding this argument helps us see how some Western thinkers advocate for knowledge unity.

Guided Path
1
Identify Maslow's historical diagnosis
Find in the passage what Maslow says about the 19th-century atheist's error. He 'burned the house instead of having mercy on it' by throwing away all questions and answers because the clergy's answers were unconvincing.
This is a key metaphor: rejecting the baby with the bathwater.
2
Extract his proposed solution
Maslow proposes expanding the concept of science so that religious questions about origin, existence, and destiny are treated as legitimate scientific issues. Scientists should not turn their backs on these inquiries.
The solution is epistemological: widen the scope of science.
3
Analyze the psychological claim
Maslow asserts that naturalistic and humanistic psychologists now consider anyone who does not care about religion as abnormal and sick. This is a strong claim linking psychological health to engagement with religious questions.
This is not a universal view but Maslow's own school of thought.
4
Evaluate the epistemological shift
Reflect on why Maslow calls these questions 'scientific issues' despite their religious nature. He grounds this in human nature: these questions are deeply rooted in human nature and therefore deserve full scientific respect.
This challenges the positivist dismissal of religion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانيا : لقد خفت تلك النظرة التي كانت تعدّ العلم والدين عالمين منفصلين عن بعضهما بالنظر إلى الأسباب الموضوعية التي أدت إلى ذلك الصراع في أوروبا في قرونها الوسطى. وليس بالضرورة أن يمثل ذلك مشكلة دينية على الدوام، بشهادة بعض الباحثين الغربيين أنفسهم . فهذا (ابراهام ماسلو) - على سبيل المثال - وهو أستاذ مشهور في علم النفس على مستوى القارة الأمريكية وخارجها، وصاحب مدرسة خاصة في ذلك، وصاحب نظرية (القوة الثالثة) في علم النفس، التي قالت عنها بعض المجلات المتخصصة من الآن وحتى قرن من الزمان، ربما سيكون أكثر النظريات موجهة لسلوكنا هي مقررات ماسلو، وليس فرويد أو دارون أو اسكين)(۲). لقد طرح ماسلو مبدأ توسيع مفهوم العلم حتى لا تتكرر مأساة ملحـد القرن التاسع عشر، الذي أحرق البيت بدلاً من أن يرحمه، حيث رمى بجميع الأسئلة وبإجاباتها معا وأدار ظهره لكل مقررات الدين نتيجة الإجابات غير المقنعة لرجال الدين حينذاك. أما اليوم فإن المفترض أن يكون رجل العلم أكثر معرفة واستنارة، فإنه وإن لم يقتنع بتلك الإجابات الدينية، لكنه لا يستطيع أن يدير ظهره لمباحث حول النشأة والوجود ،والمصير، إذ مثل هذه المباحث قضايا علمية تستحق الاحترام الكامل، لأنها ليست مجردة عن الطبيعة الإنسانية، بل هي عميقة الجذور فيها. إن الكنيسة إذا أخطأت في إجاباتها فلا يعني ذلك أنَّ الأسئلة ذاتها لا تستحق القبول والتدبّر الكاملين ومن المسلَّم به الآن - يقول ماسلو - أن علماء النفس الطبيعيين والإنسانيين سوف يعتبرون كل شخص لا يهتم بالدين وموضوعاته وقضاياه إنما هو إنسان شاذ ومريض(١).
Secondly, that view which considered science and religion as two separate worlds has diminished due to the objective reasons that led to that conflict in Europe in the Middle Ages. It is not necessarily that it represents a religious problem always, as witnessed by some Western researchers themselves. This is Abraham Maslow – for example – a famous professor of psychology in the American continent and beyond, and the founder of a special school in that field, and the author of the (third force) theory in psychology, about which some specialized journals have said that from now until a century from now, perhaps the most influential theory on our behavior will be Maslow's principles, not Freud, Darwin, or Skinner. Maslow proposed the principle of expanding the concept of science so that the tragedy of the 19th century atheist is not repeated, who burned the house instead of having mercy on it, as he threw away all questions and their answers together and turned his back on all religious teachings as a result of the unconvincing answers of the clergy at that time. Today, however, it is assumed that the scientist is more knowledgeable and enlightened, so even if he is not convinced by those religious answers, he cannot turn his back on inquiries about origin, existence, and destiny, for such inquiries are scientific issues that deserve full respect, because they are not abstracted from human nature, but are deeply rooted in it. If the Church erred in its answers, it does not mean that the questions themselves do not deserve full acceptance and reflection. It is now accepted – Maslow says – that naturalistic and humanistic psychologists will consider any person who does not care about religion and its topics and issues as an abnormal and sick human being.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage presents Abraham Maslow's epistemological argument against separating science and religion. It begins by noting that the historical conflict between science and religion in medieval Europe has cooled, and that Western thinkers like Maslow have called for integration. Maslow criticizes the 19th-century atheist for discarding all religious questions because the answers were unsatisfactory. He argues that scientists today should be wiser: even if they reject religious answers, they must respect questions about origin, existence, and destiny because these are deeply rooted in human nature. Maslow goes further, claiming that psychologists now consider disinterest in religion as pathological. The author uses Maslow's authority to support the idea of knowledge unity.

القوة الثالثة

Key Takeaway
Maslow argues that science must embrace religious questions as legitimate scientific inquiries, and that ignoring them is a sign of psychological abnormality.
