The Logical Problem of God as Source vs Revelation as Tool
Author questions the distinction between God as source and revelation as tool

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical problem in distinguishing between God as the source of knowledge and revelation as a tool, and evaluate whether this distinction is meaningful.

Core Idea
If all knowledge from God comes through revelation, then revelation is not just a tool—it is the actual source.

This passage raises a sharp logical question: if God is the ultimate source of all knowledge, and revelation is merely a 'tool' to receive it, does that distinction hold? The author argues that since we only know God's knowledge through revelation (especially the Quran), the two cannot be separated in a clean way. This is not a minor semantic point—it affects how we understand the very foundation of Islamic epistemology and the role of divine communication in acquiring knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the distinction being challenged
Find the claim that some scholars make: God is the source of knowledge, and revelation is one of its tools. Note the author's observation that this is described as a 'tendency toward conciseness' and not necessarily intended as an exclusive distinction.
2
Pinpoint the logical problem
The author asks: if we derive knowledge from God only through revelation, then how can revelation be a mere 'tool' while God is the 'source'? This suggests a redundancy or at least an unclear boundary.
The logical issue is that if revelation is the exclusive means of receiving divine knowledge, then revelation functions as the de facto source, not just a tool.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
The author quotes Quran 42:51 to show that divine communication occurs only through revelation, behind a veil, or by an angel. This supports the idea that all knowledge from God reaches humans via revelation, undermining the source–tool separation.
The verse is used to argue that revelation is the actual channel, not an optional instrument.
4
Evaluate the researcher's resolution
The passage mentions a researcher who resolves the issue by stating that all knowledge originates from God as Creator and Teacher, with senses and intellect being created tools. This reframes the problem: God is the ultimate cause, while all means are secondary.
This resolution attempts to preserve God's primacy while acknowledging the role of intermediaries.

الباب الثالث مقدمة
ومن جهة أخرى فإن بعضهم يميل إلى الإجمال في ذكر مصدر المعرفة، فيجعله واحداً ممثلاً في (الله) سبحانه وتعالى(۱) . وإنما تم وصف ذلك بأنه ميل إلى الإجمال لأنهم لا يعنون بذلك الحصر، بدليل أن بعضهم عاد في موضع آخر فذكر الوحي، تحت عنوان (أدوات المعرفة)(۲).
والسؤال المنطقي: كيف يكون (الله) مصدراً للمعرفة، والوحي أداة لها؟ وهل نستقي من الله - جل جلاله - معرفتنا إلا عن طريق وحيه لنبيه ممثلاً في القرآن الكريم قبل أي مصدر آخر؟
وهذا السؤال عينه يطرح على من ميّز بين (الله) - جل جلاله - وبين الوحي القرآن الكريم وعده مصدرًا ثانيًا لها (۳). ترى هل هناك ثمة فرق أيضاً؟ أو ليس الله تعالى هو مصدر المعرفة وقد أوحى بالقرآن إلى نبيه محمد - - بواحدة من صور الوحي الثلاث: وما كانَ لِبَشَرِ أَنْ يُكَلِّمَهُ اللهُ إِلَّا وَحْيا أَوْ مِنْ وَرَاءِ حِجَابٍ أَوْ يُرْسِلَ رَسُولاً فَيُوحِيَ بِإِذْنِهِ مَا يَشَاءُ [الشورى: ٥١/٤٢].
وإلى هذا المعنى الذي تمت الإشارة إليه من كون هناك إجمال في ذكر مصدر كلي هو الله تعالى ذهب أحد الباحثين في تفسيره لهذا المعنى إلى أن أصل المعارف كلها يعود إلى الله - سبحانه - فهو الذي خلق وعلّم. ومـا الحـس والعقل إلا جزءا من مخلوقات الله - تعالى - ولذلك فالإنسان مدين لله - تعالى - في أصل خلقه، وعارف مدين لله - تعالى - في أصل معرفته (٤).
(۱) من هؤلاء على سبيل المثال: محمد الداودي، التراث الإسلامي أداة نقد للمعرفة المعاصرة حول طبيعة الإنسان، ۱۱۱ وسيد سجاد حسين وسيد علي أشرف أزمة التعليم الإسلامي، ۲۹ - ۳۰ والكيلاني، فلسفة التربية الإسلامية، ٢٢٢.
(۲) كما فعل الكيلاني مثلاً، المرجع السابق، ۲۳۲.
(۳) كما فعل محمد الحسن بريمة، مرجع سابق، ٢٤ - ٢٩ . (٤) الكردي، مرجع سابق، ٥٢٠.
Chapter Three Introduction
On the other hand, some tend to be concise in mentioning the source of knowledge, making it one represented by (Allah) Almighty. This was described as a tendency toward conciseness because they do not mean by that exclusivity, as evidence that some of them returned in another place and mentioned revelation, under the title (Tools of Knowledge).
The logical question: How is (Allah) a source of knowledge, while revelation is a tool for it? Do we derive our knowledge from Allah Almighty except through His revelation to His Prophet, represented in the Holy Quran, before any other source?
And this same question is posed to those who distinguished between (Allah) Almighty and the revelation of the Holy Quran and counted it as a second source for it. Do you think there is a difference as well? Or is not Allah Almighty the source of knowledge, and He revealed the Quran to His Prophet Muhammad - - by one of the three forms of revelation: "And it is not for any human that Allah should speak to him except by revelation or from behind a veil or by sending a messenger to reveal by His permission what He wills" [al-Shura 42:51].
And to this meaning that was referred to, that there is conciseness in mentioning a universal source which is Allah Almighty, one researcher went in his interpretation of this meaning to say that the origin of all knowledge goes back to Allah - glorified be He - for He created and taught. And the senses and intellect are only part of Allah's creations - the Almighty - and therefore man is indebted to Allah Almighty in the origin of his creation, and a knower is indebted to Allah Almighty in the origin of his knowledge (4).
(1) For example, these include: Muhammad al-Dawudi, al-Turath al-Islami... etc. (2) As did al-Kilani, for example, previous reference, p. 232. (3) As did Muhammad al-Hasan Barima, previous reference, pp. 24-29. (4) al-Kurdi, previous reference, p. 520.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological critique. The author identifies a logical problem in the way some scholars describe God as the sole source of knowledge while relegating revelation to the status of a 'tool' (أداة). The author argues that this distinction is ambiguous because if all knowledge from God comes exclusively through revelation (the Quran), then the distinction between source and tool collapses—revelation is the de facto source. The author quotes the Quranic verse (42:51) to show that revelation is the means of divine communication. The footnote cites scholars who hold this view. The passage then mentions a researcher who resolves the issue by stating that all knowledge originates from God as Creator and Teacher, and that senses and intellect are merely created instruments, thus humans are indebted to God for both their existence and knowledge. This passage highlights a key epistemological debate in contemporary Islamic thought: the relationship between God as ultimate source and the various means of acquiring knowledge.

Key Terms
الله
الوحي
أدوات المعرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What logical problem does the author identify with the claim that God is the source of knowledge and revelation is its tool?
A) God cannot be a source at all.
B) If revelation is the only way to receive knowledge from God, then the distinction collapses because revelation is the actual means.
C) The Quran is not a valid source of knowledge.
D) Reason is superior to revelation.

Key Takeaway
In Islamic epistemology, one must carefully distinguish between the ultimate source (God) and the immediate means (revelation), or risk logical inconsistency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the statement: 'The Sunnah is a secondary source of Islamic law, while the Quran is the primary source.' Apply the same logical problem: if all rulings must trace back to the Quran, does the Sunnah become a mere tool rather than an independent source? Explain your reasoning using the passage's approach.
?
Find a contemporary Muslim scholar who distinguishes between God as source and revelation as tool. Write a short critique of that position using the logical question raised in this lesson.

The Binary Classification: Revelation and Cosmos
Author presents the binary classification of revelation and cosmos.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two sources in the binary classification according to some pioneers of the Islamization of Knowledge school and explain how they are integrated through the methodology of combining the two readings.

Core Idea
Revelation and cosmos are the two integrated sources of knowledge for civilizational witness.

In this lesson, we explore the binary classification of knowledge sources as proposed by certain figures in the Islamization of Knowledge movement. This classification presents revelation and the cosmos as the two fundamental sources, working together to guide human understanding. Understanding this classification is essential for grasping the epistemological foundations of this contemporary Islamic intellectual project.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sources
Find the phrase 'الوحي والكون هما مصدرا المعرفة الإنسانية' in the passage. Note that revelation and the cosmos are explicitly named as the two sources of human knowledge.
2
Understand the integration
The passage describes these sources as 'متكامل متضافر' (integrated and cooperative) to achieve civilizational witness and vicegerency. Reflect on how reading revelation and reading the universe complement each other.
The methodology is called 'الجمع بين القراءتين' (combining the two readings).
3
Consider the auxiliary variant
Note the variant within the binary classification that divides sources into a primary part (revelation, inspiration, intuition) and an auxiliary part (senses, reason, experience). Compare this to the main variant.
This shows flexibility within the classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تصنيف المصادر والطرائق .
تختلف وجهات الباحثين في تصنيف مصادر المعرفة وطرائقها، وبوسعنا تصنيف هذه الوجهات على النحو التالي:
التصنيف الثنائي
ينسب هذا التصنيف إلى بعض (۱) رموز مدرسة (إسلامية المعرفة) حيث يصرّح بعض رواد هذا الاتجاه بأن الوحي والكون هما مصدرا المعرفة الإنسانية، على نحو متكامل متضافر لإيصال الإنسان إلى معارف الشهود الحضاري والقيام بمهام الاستخلاف في الكون. وذلك منبثق من خلال منهج الجمع بين القراءاتين (قراءة الوحي وقراءة الكون) (۲).
ويندرج في إطار التصنيف الثنائي هذا؛ ذلك التصنيف الذي يجمل المصادر والطرائق في شق أساسي هو الوحي والإلهام والحدس وبه يعرف عالم الغيب؛ وشق مساعد للأساسي وهو الحس والعقل والتجربة (هكذا) (۳). ولكن ذلك لا أن ثمة اتفاقاً دقيقاً حتى داخل مدرسة إسلامية المعرفة) فيقضي على النزاع الناشب في إطار ذوي التصنيف الثنائي أنفسهم. ذلك أن نصا تحتويه أبرز وثيقة لهذه المدرسة يشايع التصنيف الثنائي في المجمل، بيد أنه يختلف مع القول بأن الوحي والكون هما وحدهما مصدرا المعرفة، بل الوحي والعقل هما المصدران المتكاملان، فلا مجال للتعارض بينهما (٤) . وبذلك يظهر الاختلاف حتى داخل هذه المدرسة. ومن طرائف الأمور أن يذهب أحد الباحثين في
(۱) تحديد (بعض) مقصود هنا، إذ ليس كل رموز هذه المدرسة يوافقون على هذا، كما سيرد في التصنيف الثلاثي.
(۲) طه العلواني، الجمع بين القراءتين: قراءة الوحي وقراءة الكون ٥٤ والأزمة الفكرية المعاصرة، ١٤، ٣١.
(۳) الشيباني، فلسفة التربية الإسلامية، ١٩٤.
(٤) المعهد العالمي للفكر الإسلامي، إسلامية المعرفة، ١١٥.
Classification of Sources and Methods.
The viewpoints of researchers differ in classifying the sources of knowledge and its methods, and we can classify these viewpoints as follows:
The Binary Classification
This classification is attributed to some (1) figures of the (Islamization of Knowledge) school, where some pioneers of this trend declare that revelation and the cosmos are the two sources of human knowledge, in an integrated and cooperative manner to bring man to the knowledge of civilizational witness and to fulfill the tasks of vicegerency in the universe. This emerges from the methodology of combining the two readings (reading revelation and reading the cosmos) (2).
And within the framework of this binary classification falls that classification which summarizes the sources and methods into a primary part which is revelation, inspiration, and intuition, and by it the unseen world is known; and an auxiliary part to the primary, which is the senses, reason, and experience (3). But that does not [?] that there is precise agreement even within the (Islamization of Knowledge) school, which would settle the conflict within the framework of those with the binary classification themselves. That is because a text contained in the most prominent document of this school supports the binary classification in general, but it disagrees with the statement that revelation and the cosmos alone are the two sources of knowledge; rather, revelation and reason are the two integrated sources, and there is no room for contradiction between them (4). Thus, the difference appears even within this school. And among the curious things is that one researcher goes into...
(1) The specification of (some) is intended here, as not all figures of this school agree on this, as will be mentioned in the tripartite classification. (2) Taha al-Alwani, al-Jam' bayn al-Qira'atayn... (3) al-Shaybani, Falsafat al-Tarbiya al-Islamiyya, p. 194. (4) International Institute of Islamic Thought, Islamiyyat al-Ma'rifa, p. 115.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage classifies the different viewpoints on the sources of knowledge according to scholars, focusing on one specific classification: the binary classification. The author describes that some proponents of the 'Islamization of Knowledge' school hold that the two sources are revelation (الوحي) and the cosmos (الكون), derived from the methodology of 'reading revelation and reading the universe.' The author then notes a variant within the same classification: some scholars divide sources into a primary part (revelation, inspiration, intuition) and an auxiliary part (senses, reason, experience). The passage then highlights an internal disagreement: the most prominent document of the school, while supporting a binary classification in general, replaces 'cosmos' with 'reason,' stating that revelation and reason are the two integrated sources with no contradiction. This shows a lack of precise agreement even within the same school. The footnotes provide references for each variant. The passage ends mid-sentence, cutting off before mentioning a third researcher's view.

Key Terms
التصنيف الثنائي
الوحي والكون
الجمع بين القراءتين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the binary classification attributed to some members of the Islamization of Knowledge school, what are the two sources of human knowledge?
A) Revelation and reason
B) Revelation and the cosmos (universe)
C) Senses and intellect
D) Revelation and intuition

Key Takeaway
The binary classification of knowledge sources into revelation and the cosmos is a foundational idea in the Islamization of Knowledge school, emphasizing the integration of divine guidance and empirical study.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Based on the passage, write a short paragraph explaining how revelation and the cosmos are used together to produce knowledge according to the binary classification. Use the exact terms from the passage.

The Internal Disagreement: Cosmos vs Reason
Author highlights internal disagreement over the second source.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two variants of the binary classification within the Islamization of Knowledge school: one that pairs revelation with the cosmos and another that pairs revelation with reason.

Core Idea
Even within the binary classification, the second source is contested: cosmos or reason?

While the binary classification seems straightforward, the passage reveals a significant internal disagreement. The most prominent document of the Islamization of Knowledge school rejects the pairing of revelation with the cosmos and instead pairs revelation with reason. This lesson examines this divergence and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Locate the disagreement
Find the sentence starting with 'ولكن ذلك لا أن ثمة اتفاقاً دقيقاً' (But that does not mean there is precise agreement). Identify the point of contention.
The phrase indicates a lack of consensus.
2
Identify the two positions
One position (from some pioneers) says revelation + cosmos. The other (from the IIIT document) says revelation + reason. Note the shift from cosmos to reason.
Both are binary classifications, but the second source differs.
3
Understand the reasoning
The document argues that revelation and reason are the two integrated sources with no contradiction. Reflect on why reason might replace cosmos.
This emphasizes rational coherence.

Classification of Sources and Methods.
The viewpoints of researchers differ in classifying the sources of knowledge and its methods, and we can classify these viewpoints as follows:
The Binary Classification
This classification is attributed to some (1) figures of the (Islamization of Knowledge) school, where some pioneers of this trend declare that revelation and the cosmos are the two sources of human knowledge, in an integrated and cooperative manner to bring man to the knowledge of civilizational witness and to fulfill the tasks of vicegerency in the universe. And within the framework of this binary classification falls that classification which summarizes the sources and methods into a primary part which is revelation, inspiration, and intuition, and by it the unseen world is known; and an auxiliary part to the primary, which is the senses, reason, and experience (3). But that does not [?] that there is precise agreement even within the (Islamization of Knowledge) school, which would settle the conflict within the framework of those with the binary classification themselves. That is because a text contained in the most prominent document of this school supports the binary classification in general, but it disagrees with the statement that revelation and the cosmos alone are the two sources of knowledge; rather, revelation and reason are the two integrated sources, and there is no room for contradiction between them (4). Thus, the difference appears even within this school. And among the curious things is that one researcher goes into...
